<user_id>117436908835349611687</user_id><user_name>Andre Cooper</user_name><time>1490056987373< /time><rate>2< /rate>< Review>
Ali Baba has all the makings for a great restaurant experience. The owners have really taken the time to decorate ever inch of the place. From the great flooring to the matching colors thru out. The right music playing, even the bathrooms are really done nicely. So what happened to the food and the service? Why is the place empty?

My wife and I were really shocked to discover that the food was bland and some of it old. The plating is done fairly well, with the portion sizes fair. (See photos) The meat in the kebob combo was cook great, but was bland. No flavor at all. The garlic potatoes were old and dried out. The garlic sauce was bland. The Kebbeh was excellent! The hummas was ok. And the fatoush salad was just over season sumac no flavor of mint, lemon or parsley.

The waitress was cold and distant, but she was cleaning and doing side work. Maybe she just shes defeated by an empty place. She only came to our table to drop off the food. We even had to put our order thru a machine on the table. Where is the hospitality?  When it was time to pay she never thanked us or asked us how everything was.

Its really sad that Ali Baba wasnt what we wanted it to be. We wont be back sadly as we still search for the great Lebanese restaurant.</Review>

We followed the sign a little back patio, and came across hands-down the cutest coffee shop I have ever seen. We are both crazy coffee nuts, and we have travelled the world (Germany, Armenia, Dubai, Greece, several states) looking for great coffee shops. This place easily makes the top 5 list. Easily.

I‚Äôm not a fan of non dairy options, so when the owner, AC, told us everything was dairy free, I was worried I wouldn‚Äôt like the taste. He recommended trying oat milk, because it‚Äôs the closest to dairy options. My husband got a cappuccino with almond milk, and I got myself an oat milk 24k chocolate latte.

The drinks are delicious. Seriously delicious. I could not tell that my drink was missing dairy.

We also bought a cute little Coffee & Plants pin, something to take home, and I wanted to spend more money in the cafe.

I cannot begin to explain how cute this place is. It‚Äôs a little tight, and finding parking is a pain, but once you‚Äôre inside it‚Äôs hard to want to leave. Highly recommend and I‚Äôll definitely be back.

< review>
Good coffee spot that's probably way better when itt's not covid. The drinks were great but the atmosphere of the shop and the instagrammableness of the drinks are probably much more appealing than the flavors of the drinks themselves.

They had some pretty unique coffee drinks with gold, lavendar, and other flavors but they seemed a bit overpriced for a take out drink. Came to support the business during the hard time and try something new but can't wait to be able to sit down outside in the patio and hang out with friends.

Parking really isn't great in the area, but there's a garage with one hour free near the apple store around the corner and metered street parking on side streets.

Can't wait to try this place again soon!< /review>

< Review>
Service was impeccable. We had a party of 15 and they had over 3 servers handling our group which made ordering a breeze. Everything in the sampler was delicious with the exception of the loaded potatoes which were okay. I had the bacon wrapped filet dinner with salad. The first bites were delicious then the over-seasoning hit me, I recommend ordering it lightly seasoned if that's possible and probably medium rare since mine was medium and there was no pink in the center. Overall, I give this dish 3.5 stars. Ask for the dressing on the side for your salad because again it's doused with dressing. Staff was friendly and attentive which made experience overall 4 stars.<//Review>

<text>Nice afghan place in Oakland. It was my first time in Oakland and found this spot. I was gonna try this place or the Maya taqueria place next to it.

The seating is nice. I love there is a musallah so u can pray salah (we prayed Isha here post iftar) that is worth 2 stars on it's own.

The food was okay. The brown rice tastes like basmati with color. Not much zing to the flavor of the rice. I ordered the beef chapli kabob plate

The chapli kabob was kind of small which was dissapointing (other places give you 2 big chapli kabobs). And they gave u a lemon slice and one grilled tomato(good steamed but no flavor in it)

< username>
David S Hogan<//username>
<time>1553570598725<//time><Rate>4< /Rate>< text>
Great food and friendly service. In downtown Oakland, which might scare off a few timid travelers, but, all in all, I recommend visiting.

I ordered to go, and the host told me 20 minutes for the chicken breast kabab entree. It probably took 15, and I did not mind waiting. There was a big screen TV playing music video hits from the 90s (hello, BSB!), but I suppose that's better than nothing at all.

The space is large, and if you are dining in, there's an option to sit in a special area which appears to give a more authentic Afghan dining experience (no shoes, low table).

The food was cooked to perfection, of a good portion, and the spicy cilantro (?) sauce was heaven.

Room for improvement: Men's bathroom. Things were clean enough, in appearance, but there was an unpleasant odor. Be prepared.<//text>

<Review>I love this place. This is the first time I've ever been and I have to say the food was delicious!! The menu states that everything is made in house and is made to order which results in food taking longer to come out. The wait can be from 20 to 30 minutes so if your really hungry I'd suggest you order ahead of time.

The restaurant is quite big and open. Lots of tables, capable for large parties as well as more intimate meals. It is in downtown oakland so parking can be difficult, but there is a parking lot at the end of the block.

Lastly, the pricing is fair. Meals on average run from about $11-$15 which usually includes rice and salad.< /Review>< date>

< review>
I ordered the kabob that came with rice and afghan salad. Im also an afghani who has been making these dishes since I was old enough to fold Mantu, but I found this plate disappointing. I asked them not to cook it well done preferring juicier kabobs, but it was so tough I, as well as my partner and son couldn't even take a bite from I without fearing broken teeth. Literally, it was even hard cutting it with a steak knife. The afghan salad was made cheaply because it just tasted like chopped onions with maybe three pieces of cucumber, no tomatoes, mint, lemon, salt, nothing. I ordered afghan bread naan and clarified I didn't want some pita bread you can buy at Safeway. But I still paid 3 dollars for tough pita bread and when I told her they made a mistake rather then exchanging it she handed me a bag with a tiny piece which was a rip off because I told her I was only interested in the naan. I mean I didn't tell her way later but immediately so I don't know why she did it like that. Mantu was pretty good but the serving was so tiny it was only enough for my 4 year old. I was really bummed and hope to find a good afghan restaurant around here. This was a waste of 27 dollars for 1 kabob plate and mantu. I get some white people may think this is a god send but I asure you, its not that great.</review>
